    20→### BUG: Inconsistent Error Handling for Clipboard API  
    21→**Severity**: low  
    22→**Location**: `copyInstallCommand`  
    23→**Problem**: The `copyInstallCommand` function handles errors from `navigator.clipboard.writeText` by setting a component-level `error` state. However, this `error` state is also used for build-related errors. If a clipboard error occurs, it will overwrite any existing build error message, and vice-versa. This can lead to confusion for the user, as a build error might disappear if they try to copy the command and it fails.  
    24→**Fix**: Introduce a separate state variable for clipboard-related errors, or ensure that the error message clearly indicates its source. For example, `setClipboardError('Failed to copy command to clipboard')` and display this error separately.

     7→- **Task**: Analyze the source code below for correctness bugs. This is a bash install script (AI Maestro dashboard). Check for logic errors, broken conditional logic, incorrect variable usage, race conditions, security issues, and error handling. Do NOT report style issues.  
     8→  
     9→Report each bug with format:  
    10→### BUG: <title>  
    11→**Severity**: critical|high|medium|low  
    12→**Location**: <scope>

    14→**Fix**: <fix>  
    15→

    17→  
    18→---  
    19→  
    20→### BUG: Incorrect `portable_sed` usage in `act4_start_and_register`  
    21→**Severity**: high  
    22→**Location**: `act4_start_and_register`  
    23→**Problem**: The `portable_sed` function is called with `safe_dir_repl` for the replacement string. However, `safe_dir_repl` is created by escaping characters that are special in `sed`'s *regex pattern*, not its *replacement string*. The `sed` replacement string has its own special characters, notably `&` (which inserts the matched pattern) and `\` (which is used for backreferences or escaping `&`). If `INSTALL_DIR` contains `&` or `\`, `portable_sed` will interpret them incorrectly in the replacement string, leading to corrupted paths in `CLAUDE.md` files.  
    24→**Fix**: The `safe_dir_repl` variable needs to escape `&` and `\` specifically for the `sed` replacement string. The current `safe_dir` variable already escapes `\` for the regex pattern, but `&` needs to be escaped for the replacement string.  
    25→  
    26→```bash  
    27→# In act4_start_and_register  
    28→    local safe_dir  
    29→    safe_dir=$(printf '%s' "$INSTALL_DIR" | sed 's/[[\.*^$|&\\\/]/\\&/g'  

... [7240 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    26→  
    27→### BUG: Insecure Temporary Directory Creation  
    28→**Severity**: high  
    29→**Location**: `buildPlugin`, `scanRepo`, `pushToGitHub`  
    30→**Problem**: The `buildPlugin` function creates a build directory using `path.join(BUILDS_DIR, buildId)` where `buildId` is a `randomUUID()`. While `randomUUID()` makes the `buildId` unique, `BUILDS_DIR` is derived from `os.tmpdir()`. This pattern is vulnerable to race conditions and symlink attacks if an attacker can predict or create a symlink at the target path before the directory is created. Similarly, `scanRepo` and `pushToGitHub` use `fs.mkdtemp` which is secure, but `buildPlugin` does not.  
    31→**Fix**: Use `fs.mkdtemp`   

... [7822 more chars truncated]  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:53:04]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a clear picture of the three bugs. Let me verify each one against the actual code before fixing:  

**Bug 1** (line 1192): `safe_dir_repl` escapes `[&|]` but should only escape `&` and `\` for sed replacement strings. Current: `sed 's/[&|]/\\&/g'` — `|` is not special in sed replacement but `\` is. Fix: change to `sed 's/[&\]/\\&/g'`.  

**Bug 2** (line 1236): `${gw_list}` is used directly in the sed replacement, meaning literal `\n` sequences from the shell variable won't become actual newlines in the file. Fix: wrap with `$(printf '%b' "$gw_list")`.  

**Bug 3** (line 1113): `pm2 restart ai-maestro 2>/dev/null || pm2 restart all 2>/dev/null || true` — the `|| pm2 restart all 2>/dev/null` fallback must be removed.  

All three bugs are confirmed present. Now I'll apply the fixes.  

</div>

Fix this specific bug:  
**`buildPlugin` uses predictable temp dir**: The `buildPlugin` function creates a build directory with `const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, buildId); await fs.mkdir(buildDir, { recursive: true })`. This is vulnerable to race conditions. Fix: Replace those two lines with `const buildDir = await fs.mkdtemp(path.join(BUILDS_DIR, 'build-'))` (remove the mkdir call since mkdtemp creates the dir).  

Note: `scanRepo` and `pushToGitHub` already use `fs.mkdtemp` correctly — do NOT change those.

    19→  
    20→### BUG: Insecure Temporary Directory Usage  
    21→**Severity**: high  
    22→**Location**: BUILDS_DIR, scanRepo, pushToGitHub  
    23→**Problem**: The service uses `os.tmpdir()` to create temporary directories for builds, repo scans, and GitHub pushes. While `os.tmpdir()` is generally safe, the way the directories are named (`ai-maestro-plugin-builds`, `ai-maestro-scan-<id>`, `ai-maestro-push-<id>`) does not guarantee unique and secure directory creation. An attacker could potentially predict or race to create these directories, leading to symlink attacks or other forms of path traversal/privilege escalation if the service runs with elevated permissions. For instance, if `ai-maestro-plugin-builds` is created with predictable permissions, another process could create a symlink inside it before the service writes files, redirecting file writes to arbitrary locations.  
    24→**Fix**: Use `fs.mkdtemp` to create secure, unique temporary directories. `fs.mkdtemp` creates a unique temporary directory with a given prefix, preventing race conditions and ensuring secure permissions.  


... [7686 more chars truncated]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 19:53:10]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the exact picture. The findings report confirms:  

1. **Bug 1 (path traversal in `validateBuildConfig`)**: Already fixed - lines 169-176 already have the `SAFE_PATH_SEGMENT_RE` checks for both `skill.marketplace` and `skill.plugin`. No change needed.  

2. **Bug 2 (insecure temp dirs)**: Confirmed - line 438 uses `path.join(os.tmpdir(), \`ai-maestro-scan-${scanId}\`)` and line 505 uses `path.join(os.tmpdir(), \`ai-maestro-push-${pushId}\`)`. These need to be changed to `fs.mkdtemp`.  

The key concern with the `mkdtemp` change is that both `scanDir` and `pushDir` are used in the `catch` block's cleanup. With `mkdtemp`, the directory is created by the call itself, so cleanup in `catch` is still valid. However, I must also ensure the `git clone` target path is handled correctly — `git clone` requires the target directory to NOT exist, but `mkdtemp` creates it. I need to verify this before applying the fix.  

</div>

    20→### BUG: Inconsistent `description` handling in `buildConfig`  
    21→**Severity**: low  
    22→**Location**: `PluginBuilderPage`  
    23→**Problem**: The `description` field in `buildConfig` is explicitly set to `undefined` if it's an empty string. However, the `PluginComposer` component, which also uses this `description` state, might expect an empty string for its input field. While `undefined` and `''` are often treated similarly in React inputs, this explicit conversion could lead to subtle inconsistencies or unexpected behavior if downstream components or the build process differentiate between an empty string and an undefined value for `description`. It's generally better to maintain consistency in data types unless there's a specific reason for the conversion.  
    24→**Fix**: Remove the `|| undefined` part from the `description` field in the `buildConfig` `useMemo` hook. Let `description` be an empty string if the user hasn't entered anything, which is its initial state.

    20→### BUG: Inconsistent Error Handling for Clipboard API  
    21→**Severity**: low  
    22→**Location**: `copyInstallCommand`  
    23→**Problem**: The `copyInstallCommand` function handles errors from `navigator.clipboard.writeText` by setting a component-level `error` state. However, this `error` state is also used for build-related errors. If a clipboard error occurs, it will overwrite any existing build error message, and vice-versa. This can lead to confusion for the user, as a build error might disappear if they try to copy the command and it fails.  
    24→**Fix**: Introduce a separate state variable for clipboard-related errors, or ensure that the error message clearly indicates its source. For example, `setClipboardError('Failed to copy command to clipboard')` and display this error separately.  
    25→  
    26→### BUG: Potential Race Condition in Polling Logic  
    27→**Severity**: medium  
    28→**Location**: `handleBuild`

    16→If no bugs found, respond with exactly: NO ISSUES FOUND  
    17→  
    18→---  
    19→  
    20→### BUG: Missing dependency in `useEffect` for `load` function  
    21→**Severity**: high  
    22→**Location**: `SkillPicker` component, `useEffect` hook for loading marketplace skills  
    23→**Problem**: The `useEffect` hook that fetches marketplace skills does not include `setMarketplaceSkills` and `setLoadingMarketplace` in its dependency array. While these are state setters and generally stable, in some React versions or future React behaviors, omitting them could lead to stale closures if they were to be recreated. More critically, the `load` function itself is defined inside `useEffect` and uses these setters. If `load` were to be moved outside or if the setters were to change identity (unlikely for `useState` setters but good practice), this could lead to issues.  
    24→**Fix**: Add `setMarketplaceSkills` and `setLoadingMarketplace` to the dependency array of the `useEffect` hook.  
    25→  
    26→```typescript  
    27→// ... (inside SkillPicker component)  
    28→  useEffect(() => {  
    29→    abortRef.current = new AbortController()  
    30→    const signal = abortRef.current.signal  
  

... [3820 more chars truncated]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:04:12]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have a complete picture. Let me catalog all the places where `await` is missing. The key distinction is:  

- Functions returning `ServiceResult<T>` (sync) - no `await` needed  
- Functions returning `Promise<ServiceResult<T>>` (async) - `await` is needed  

Based on my research:  

**Teams service** - ALL are SYNC (no `async` prefix): `listAllTeams`, `createNewTeam`, `getTeamById`, `updateTeamById`, `deleteTeamById`, `listTeamTasks`, `createTeamTask`, `updateTeamTask`, `deleteTeamTask`, `listTeamDocuments`, `createTeamDocument`, `getTeamDocument`, `updateTeamDocument`, `deleteTeamDocument` - these do NOT need `await`.

- None in messages-service meetings functions (all sync)  
- None in webhooks/domains (all sync)  

But wait - I need to re-examine more carefully. The `sendServiceResult` function's signature is `sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any)`. If a Promise is passed as `result`, the function will call `result.error` on a Promise object — which will be `undefined`, and `result.data` will also be `undefined`, so it will try `result.status || 200` which on a Promise is also undefined, giving `200`, and then `JSON.stringify(result.data)` = `JSON.stringify(undefined)` = `undefined` causing issues.  

The findings report from the LLM correctly identified these as bugs because these functions SHOULD have `await`. The fact that they are declared as sync functions in the service files is the current state — but that may be incorrect too. Let me verify by checking what they actually DO internally.

/**  
 * Create a new team.  
 */  
export function createNewTeam(params: CreateTeamParams): ServiceResult<{ team: any }> {  
  const { name, description, agentIds } = params  

  if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') {  
    return { error: 'Team name is required', status: 400 }  
  }  

  if (agentIds && !Array.isArray(agentIds)) {  
    return { error: 'agentIds must be an array', status: 400 }  
  }

    const team = createTeam({ name, description, agentIds: agentIds || [] })  
    return { data: { team }, status: 201 }  
  } catch (error) {  
    console.error('Failed to create team:', error)  
    return { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to create team', status: 500 }  
  }  
}

export function listMeetings(statusFilter?: string | null): ServiceResult<{ meetings: any[] }> {  
  let meetings = loadMeetings()  
  if (statusFilter) {  
    meetings = meetings.filter(m => m.status === statusFilter)  
  }  
  return { data: { meetings }, status: 200 }  
}  

// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
// Meetings: POST /api/meetings  
// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  

export interface CreateMeetingParams {  
  name: string  
  agentIds: string[]  
  teamId?: string | null  
  sidebarMode?: SidebarMode  
}  

export function createNewMeeting(  
  params: CreateMeetingParams,  
): ServiceResult<{ meeting: any }> {  
  const { name, agentIds, teamId, sidebarMode } = params  

  if (!name || typeof name !== 'string') {  
    return { error: 'Meeting name is required', status: 400 }  
  }  

  if (!agentIds || !Array.isArray(agentIds) || agentIds.length === 0) {  
    return { error: 'At least one agent is required', status: 400 }  
  }  

  try {  
    const meeting = createMeeting({  
      name,  
      agentIds,  
      teamId: teamId || null,  
      sidebarMode,  
    })  
    return { data: { meeting }, status: 201 }  
  } catch (error) {  
    console.error('Failed to create meeting:', error)  
    return {  
      error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to create meeting',  
      status: 500,  
    }  
  }  
}  

// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
// Meetings: GET /api/meetings/[id]  
// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  

export function getMeetingById(id: string): ServiceResult<{ meeting: any }> {  
  const meeting = getMeeting(id)  
  if (!meeting) {  
    return { error: 'Meeting not found', status: 404 }  
  }  
  return { data: { meeting }, status: 200 }  
}
